Rural Life Miscellany

— Pan Yiyun

The Life of Silk Farmers in Shunde, Guangdong

General Social Background

Friends! When you board a steamer and leave Guangzhou, heading south along the West River for about two hours, you will arrive at Shunde County. Geographically, Shunde is located in the center of a delta in the lower reaches of the Pearl River. It borders Panyu County to the northeast, Zhongshan County to the southeast, Xinhui County to the southwest, and Nanhai County to the northwest. The area is mostly flat plains and slightly low-lying, with fertile soil, crisscrossed by waterways, making transportation very convenient. According to the statistics of the 19th year of the Republic of China (1930), the total population of Shunde County is over 1,426,000, living in 214 villages. Most of the people rely on silkworm farming as their main production activity, numbering about one million.

The Dwellings of Silk Farmers

Upon arriving in Shunde, what first catches the eye is probably the dwellings of the silk farmers. Generally, ordinary silk farmers live near the mulberry fields, clustered together in clans, ranging from a few families to dozens, in groups that may extend for miles or gather in one corner. The construction of their houses is very simple, with mud walls and thatched roofs everywhere. The interior naturally has a dirt floor, with very few windows, making it poorly ventilated and dimly lit. Their bedrooms and silkworm rearing rooms are mostly mixed and undivided, with silkworms and people crowded together, making their cramped conditions imaginable. There are also some poor silk farmers who migrate constantly, their dwellings scattered among the mulberry fields, built temporarily by themselves, naturally even more simple than the aforementioned type. From a distance, one only sees scattered thatched huts, appearing and disappearing among the mulberry bushes, arousing thoughts of the early days of primitive society.

The Farmland of Silk Farmers

The silk farmers in Shunde cultivate many mulberry fields themselves, usually adjacent to or near their residences. The area they cultivate varies in size, averaging from two to twenty mu at most. According to statistical reports, each silk farming household cultivates an average of 7.22 mu of mulberry fields, but over 92% of the land is rented from landlords. The rent per mu ranges from eight to forty yuan, depending on the size of the fish pond area and the fertility of the land. Commonly calculated, if fish ponds account for 29% of the mulberry field area, the annual rent per mu is twenty-one yuan. Here, the terms "fish pond" and "mulberry field" need to be clarified. Because the terrain in the silkworm-producing areas of Guangdong is low-lying, silk farmers manage mulberry fields using the "four parts water, six parts land" system. For example, in ten mu of mulberry fields, four mu should be used for fish ponds. Those who come to Shunde for the first time, seeing clear pond water and green mulberry fields everywhere, cannot help but feel a unique pastoral charm.

The Work of Silk Farmers

Their main work is naturally planting mulberry trees and raising silkworms. Around mid-March each year, silkworm rearing begins, involving the entire family. Generally, strong men and women are responsible for picking mulberry leaves and feeding silkworms, while elderly women and children engage in picking silkworms, collecting cocoons, reeling silk, and assisting with household chores. Because Guangdong has a mild climate, silkworm rearing can be done six or seven times a year. During the busiest times, they lack even sleep. Speaking of which, we must mention the issue of technology. Although the silk farmers are diligent, their production techniques, from silkworm rearing to silk reeling and silk weaving, are unreasonable, outdated, and unscientific. How to improve them in the future is a problem that urgently needs to be solved. In addition to silkworm rearing, fish farming is their main sideline. They use silkworm excrement, silkworm pupae, and silkworm moths as fish feed and can also use the mud from the ponds to enrich the mulberry fields, making it a quite worthwhile sideline.

The Education of Silk Farmers

Very few adult silk farmers in Shunde have received education. According to survey results, only nine out of one hundred people are literate, and 60-70% of school-age children are not enrolled in school. Because of the lack of education, the behavior of silk farmers often falls into superstition. When they encounter silkworm diseases or other losses during silkworm rearing, they blame ghosts and gods, trusting in fate, without making any efforts to remedy the situation. Almost every family worships the Silkworm Goddess, and many also rely on stone and clay idols for protection. What we see in the silkworm villages, whether in street corners or alleyways, are piles of stone pebbles, surrounded by incense smoke. This is their patron saint, the master of their souls. What a serious education problem this is!

The Health of Silk Farmers

From our superficial observations, we can naturally see that the health of Shunde silk farmers is not good. According to a survey of the health of 105 families in the Shunde Sericulture Improvement Implementation Area in the 22nd year of the Republic of China (1933), the statistics showed a population of 457 people, of whom 133 were unhealthy. In the same year, a survey of infant mortality in 100 families showed that out of 582 children born, 234 died. Furthermore, according to the treatment report for October of this year from the general district of the implementation area, in one month, 88 patients sought treatment for skin diseases, 80 for ear, nose, and throat diseases, 94 for internal medicine, 132 for surgery, 8 for parasitic diseases, 4 for dental diseases, 75 for red eye and other diseases, and 2 were hospitalized, totaling 397 people. The population under the jurisdiction of the general district is only about four to five thousand. Therefore, the health status of silk farmers is self-evident.

The Economic Income of Silk Farmers

In the past, Shunde was a very wealthy county. In the 11th year of the Republic of China (1922), the export value of raw silk from Guangdong Province was over 110 million yuan, most of which was handled by the people of Shunde. At that time, they were the fortunate ones, living a life of extreme affluence, feasting, celebrating, singing, and dancing. But since the world economic crisis, the price of silk has plummeted; and because their production technology is too backward, they have lost the market. The entire silk industry in the county has been declining day by day, and today it is in a state of bankruptcy. According to a recent survey, only 4% of the silk farming households in the county can make a slight profit annually, no more than 4% can barely break even, and as many as 92% suffer losses every year. As a result, those who have dropped out of the business have dropped out, those who have lost their jobs have lost their jobs, and those who are in debt are in debt. Everyone is struggling on the brink of death.

Shunde, the life of the silk farmers of Shunde as a whole, is what is displayed to us, a picture of such sorrow and suffering.

Page 11

Local News

Chairman Chiang's Telegraphic Order Explaining the Method of Trying Opium and Drug Cases, Stipulating Seven Articles of Measures for the Municipal Government to Comply With

Amidst the vigorous anti-opium campaign in various places, the method of trying opium and drug cases has been stipulated by the highest anti-opium authority. The municipal government yesterday specially instructed the Public Security Bureau to comply with it. The full text of the instructions and the stipulated seven articles of measures are recorded below:

The telegram from the Military Commission Chairman and Anti-Opium Superintendent's Office stated, "The Provisional Regulations for the Punishment of Opium Crimes and the Provisional Regulations for the Punishment of Drug Crimes each specify the organs with military legal authority to try cases or authorize local governments at all levels to try cases on their behalf. Now, seven articles of measures for trying opium and drug cases are stipulated below: 1. The county magistrate of the place where the offender is located or where the crime was committed shall concurrently serve as a military judge of this office to try the case. 2. If the county magistrate does not concurrently serve as a military judge of this office, the county government may try the case on its behalf. If the county magistrate is concurrently the Administrative Inspector Commissioner, the Administrative Inspector Commissioner shall try the case. 3. If there is a Security Commander in the place where the crime was committed or where the offender is located, the Security Commander shall try the case in the first instance, but if there is a Pacification Director, the Pacification Commissioner's Office shall try the case in the first instance. 4. Within the municipal area, the municipal government is authorized to try cases, but if there is a Garrison Commander, the Garrison Commander shall try the case. 5. When the county government tries the case on behalf of the authorities, in addition to handling it in accordance with Articles 1, Sections 6 and 7, and Article 2 of the Measures for the Military Commission Chairman's Office Authorizing the Highest Military and Political Officers of Each Province to Review Military Legal Cases on Their Behalf, the case file and judgment shall be submitted to the provincial government for forwarding to the Chairman and Superintendent for approval and execution. 6. In the Weihaiwei Special Zone, the Commissioner's Office shall try the case. Cases discovered by the Anti-Opium Inspectorate shall be tried by the Anti-Opium Inspectorate. 7. The jurisdiction of the trial organs shall be subject to the provisions of Chapter 3 of the Criminal Procedure Law. It is hoped that you will investigate and handle this matter and forward it to your subordinates for compliance as necessary." Therefore, we should comply with the above instructions and order the bureau to comply with them and forward them to their subordinates for information. This order." After receiving the order, the Public Security Bureau also issued orders to all sub-bureaus for information.

Students of the National Conservatory of Music Petitioned Yesterday Afternoon

According to the Central News Agency, yesterday (the 21st) at 11:00 AM, more than one hundred students from the National Conservatory of Music went to the Nanfu to petition and submitted a petition regarding the North China incident. Mayor Wu was busy with official duties and could not meet with them, so he sent Section Chief Li Dachao to represent him and meet with them. First of all, he expressed his admiration for the students' enthusiasm for petitioning and decided to report the situation of the students from major middle schools who came to the government yesterday to petition, which Mayor Wu personally rectified. Then, the student representatives explained the requests: 1. Please ask the government to abolish the disguised autonomous organization in North China. 2. Maintain the integrity of territory and sovereignty. 3. Open diplomacy. 4. Protect the people's freedom of assembly and speech. 5. Effectively protect patriotic movements in various places. 6. Please order the release of the arrested students in North China and punish the military police who caused the incident. Section Chief Li answered each of them in detail and promised to forward the report. All the students felt completely satisfied and bid farewell and left.

Middle School Students Established the Save-the-Nation Joint Association Yesterday, Requesting the Central Government to Safeguard Territorial Integrity and Assist the Patriotic Movement of Students in North China

According to Shanghai News Agency, in order to promote the national patriotic spirit and assist the government in safeguarding the integrity of national territory and sovereignty, students from various middle schools in the city initiated the organization of the Shanghai Middle School Students National Salvation Joint Association. A founding meeting was held at Shanghai Girls' High School at 2:00 PM yesterday. The charter was revised, executive members were elected, and multiple resolutions were passed at the meeting. The details are recorded below:

Participating Schools: Representatives from 51 middle schools, including Guanghua, Daxia, Jingye, Minli, Pudong, Fudan, Fushi, Datong, Dagong, Chengzhong, Chizhi, Qingxin, Shanghai Normal School for Young Children, Private Shangzhong, Shanghai Girls' High School, Minli Girls' High School, Nanyang Model, Fanzhengfeng, Quanzhang, Binhai, Minguang, Jianguo, Qingnian, Xinmin, Peiming, Daozhong, Cihang, China, Aiguo, Liangjiang, China Girls' High School, Anhui, Minsheng, Guangdong, Minguo, Yuqing, Dazhong, Mingde, Junyi, Wusong, Kunfan, Kaiming, Yangjing, Dongfang, Yucai, Xinhuan, Dongnan, Zhizhong, Xinya, Hubei, etc., totaling more than one hundred students, attended.

Meeting Situation: At 2:00 PM, representatives from various schools arrived and the meeting was opened with a bell. A presidium was publicly elected from Minli, Junyi, Dagong, Private Shangzhong, China, Jingye, and Minli Girls' High School. Yuqing Middle School served as the master of ceremonies, and Shanghai Girls' High School and Qingnian Middle School served as recorders. After the formalities were completed, the presidium delivered the opening speech, stating that since the establishment of the pseudo-autonomous organization in North China, the people of the whole country have been indignant. Students in various places in Pingjing, forced by righteousness, have begun a save-the-nation movement. The middle school students in the city are enthusiastic about saving the country and dare not lag behind. They should make effective support. Therefore, they initiated the organization of the Shanghai Middle School Students National Salvation Joint Association to unify the organization, concentrate their strength, and assist the government in safeguarding the integrity of the territory and sovereignty.

Charter Adopted: The decision was made to discuss the charter. The chairman read it out item by item, and it was adopted as follows: 1. The name of this association is the Shanghai Middle School Students National Salvation Joint Association (abbreviated as Shanghai Middle School Salvation Joint Association). 2. The purpose of this association is to promote the national patriotic spirit and assist the government in safeguarding the integrity of the national territory and sovereignty. 3. This association is composed of three representatives from each middle school in Shanghai to form a representative assembly. 4. The executive committee of this association is organized by the representative assembly electing 20 executive members and 9 alternate executive members (based on schools). 5. The executive committee mutually elects 7 standing executive members, one chairman and one vice-chairman. 6. The highest authority of this association is the representative assembly, under which is the executive committee, which is responsible for the following affairs: (A) General Affairs Section, (B) Document Section, (C) Propaganda Section, (D) Liaison Section. Special committees may be established when necessary. 7. The affairs of each section are undertaken by the executive members. 8. The executive committee meets once a week, convened by the chairman. Extraordinary meetings may be convened when necessary. 9. The expenses of this association are borne by the students of the participating middle schools. Special collections may be made temporarily when necessary. 10. This charter shall be implemented upon approval by the Shanghai Middle School Students Representative Assembly. 11. Any unfinished matters shall be amended by the representative assembly.

Assembly Resolutions: Adopted as follows: 1. Telegraph the Central Government to punish Yin Rugeng, the traitor. 2. Telegraph the Central Government to implement revolutionary diplomacy. 3. Oppose any pseudo-organization in North China. 4. Request the Central Government to safeguard the integrity of territorial sovereignty. 5. Assist the patriotic movement of students in North China.

Election of Executive Members: Finally, the executive members were elected, with Shanghai Girls' High School receiving 40 votes, Qingxin Middle School 38 votes, Minli Middle School 38 votes, Wuben Girls' High School 37 votes, Kaiming Middle School 36 votes, Minli Girls' High School 35 votes, Daxia Affiliated Middle School 35 votes, Datong Affiliated Middle School 34 votes, Guanghua Affiliated Middle School 34 votes, China Girls' High School 34 votes, Qingnian Middle School 33 votes, Yuqing Middle School 32 votes, Dagong Vocational School 32 votes, Junyi 32 votes, Private Shangzhong 32 votes, Jingye Middle School 31 votes, Pudong Middle School 31 votes, Peiming Girls' High School 28 votes, Yucai Middle School 28 votes, Zhengfeng Middle School 28 votes, Aiguo Girls' High School 27 votes, Fudan Shizhong 25 votes, Minguang Middle School 24 votes, Guangdong Middle School 23 votes, Fudan Affiliated Middle School 22 votes. The above 25 schools were elected as executive members. Yangjing Junior High School 25 votes, Kunfan Girls' High School 22 votes, Hubei 21 votes, Xinhuan Vocational School 20 votes, Xinmin Middle School 20 votes, Daozhong Girls' High School 17 votes, Huashu Girls' High School 16 votes, Cihang Midwifery 15 votes, Quanzhang Middle School 13 votes. The above were elected as alternate executive members.

According to the Central News Agency, students from various places, in response to the anti-pseudo-autonomy movement of students in Peiping, petitioned and paraded to local administrative officials. The Ministry of Finance Plans to Establish Eight Major Banks. In Addition to Reorganizing the Central Bank into a Reserve Bank, Seven More Banks Will Be Established, Including Exchange, Real Estate, and Other Banks

According to New Sound News Agency, the Ministry of Finance has achieved considerable results since implementing the new currency policy. In addition to reorganizing the Central Bank into the Central Reserve Bank, it also plans to establish seven banks, including exchange, industry, industrial, agricultural, real estate, trust, and savings banks. The details are recorded below:

Meeting Held Yesterday Afternoon: The Central Bank has decided to reorganize into the Central Reserve Bank, which has been prepared by the bank's board of directors. At the same time, in accordance with Article 7 of the Central Bank Law, 40% of the shares will be raised from businesses, and legal entities in the country's banking industry will be given priority to subscribe. The bank also held a meeting of standing directors at 11:30 AM yesterday. Standing directors Kong Xianxi, Chen Jian'an, Ye Zhuotang, Xu Kan, Tang Shoumin, and others attended. The meeting adjourned at around 12:00 PM. It is reported that the meeting was to prepare for the reorganization and to convene a board of directors meeting before the end of the month to discuss everything. As for the date of the reorganization and establishment, it may have to be postponed until next spring. The saying that it would be implemented on New Year's Day, as reported in the Jing telegram, is not feasible because the preparations cannot be completed in time.

Preparation in Order: In order to help the agricultural, industrial, and commercial sectors, the Ministry of Finance has decided to reorganize the Central Bank into the Central Reserve Bank, which will become a bank for banks, and plans to establish seven banks, including exchange, industry, industrial, agricultural, trust, savings, and real estate banks, making a total of eight banks. In addition to the Bank of China, which was originally a chartered international exchange bank specializing in exchange, and the Bank of Communications, which was originally a chartered bank for developing national industries specializing in industry, other banks such as industrial and agricultural banks will be established in due course.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Advocates Using "Currency" Instead of "Silver Dollar" in Bookkeeping

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce received a letter from Xu Chongdao Guoyaohao inquiring about what character should be used above the numbers recorded in Chinese bookkeeping to represent the term "silver dollar." The Chamber immediately replied in a letter stating, "The term 'silver dollar' has always been a common term and should be reformed. In theory, the two characters 'national currency' should be used instead. As your letter states, the grid in Chinese bookkeeping is short, and the two characters 'national currency' are too inconvenient, then it seems that using only the character 'currency' is also permissible. Since the amount is marked as so many yuan and so many jiao, it is known without asking that it is the national currency and not foreign currency."

Zou Lu Visited Various Factories Yesterday and Expressed His Opinions on Developing Chinese Industry

Central Committee member Zou Lu and Hu Wencan were invited by the China Industrial Federation to visit the Zhongxin Yarn Factory, Huacheng Tobacco Company, Commercial Press, and China Machine-Made Shoe Factory yesterday morning. Afterwards, they expressed their opinions on developing Chinese industry, saying that the reason for the underdevelopment of Chinese industry is insufficient capital and too few chips for operation. Therefore, there cannot be significant progress in the improvement of technology and the increase of production. For example, setting up a factory requires a capital of one million yuan. Eight out of ten parts have been used for machine factory buildings. The cash flow that is relied on for the production part is very small. In the past, when China's credit system had not been destroyed, a small amount of capital could be used for a large amount of production, so the strength was abundant and the financial resources were not exhausted. Today is very different from the past. If you want to revitalize Chinese industry, unless you turn the factory buildings, machines, and activities into cash, when there is more capital, there will naturally be more production. As for the fundamental cure, it is still to find a way to make the people have property, so that their purchasing power can be strengthened, and then the entire Chinese production can fundamentally find a way out. When asked about the impressions he got from visiting the factory, he summarized it by saying that the textile industry is beneficial to the people's livelihood and clothing and is deeply related to the national economy. I deeply feel that under any difficult circumstances, the government must maintain the Chinese yarn industry, lighten its burden, and make it prosperous, so that it can establish a position to compete with foreign countries. There are now very large sales of yarn in the Southwest. This time I will return to Guangdong and find ways to expand its market in a short period of time, and all methods cannot be successful without the cooperation of Shanghai and Guangdong. Mr. Rong Zongjing is courageous and persevering in this difficult situation, and his spirit and perseverance are admirable. The Commercial Press was destroyed by the fire of war at the old factory site after the January 28 Incident. Today it is restored, and all scales are gradually restored to their original state. This is the result of the efforts of the factory colleagues. The new factory of Huacheng Tobacco Company is large in scale and well-equipped. The machines used are all recently purchased from abroad, so its products can compete with foreign goods. The products of the China Machine-Made Shoe Factory are completely domestic products and the price is low. In the future, with mass production, the sales will be large. It is indeed a new emerging industry in China. In short, the decline of Chinese industry has reached its extreme, but the general colleagues can still resolutely fight, so I am still optimistic about the future of China.

Municipal Party Headquarters and Other Ten Organizations Hosted a Farewell Banquet for Ambassador Cheng Yesterday

The Municipal Party Headquarters, Local Association, Banking Association, Municipal Farmers Association, Municipal Education Association, Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Municipal Federation of Trade Unions, Provisional Municipal Council, Journalists Association, Tongji University, and other organizations held a banquet at the YMCA of Eight Immortals Bridge at 6:15 pm last night to bid farewell to Ambassador to Germany Cheng Tianfang.

Participating Personnel: A total of ten organizations participated in the farewell, with guests and hosts totaling more than fifty people, including Ambassador Cheng, Chen Zehua, Zheng Xigu, Wu Xingya, Pan Gongzhan, Cai Jingjun, Wang Xiaolai, Weng Zhilong, Tong Hangbai, Wu Kaixian, Shen Tianxin, Du Yuesheng, Yu Zuoting, and Zhu Xuefan. Wu Xingya presided over the meeting and delivered a farewell speech on behalf of the organizations. Ambassador Cheng then replied, and Wang Xiaolai and Weng Zhilong also gave speeches. The meeting ended at 9 pm.

Chairman's Speech: Wu Xingya said in his speech that Ambassador Cheng has contributed to the Party and the country, and has worked hard to oppose communism since the 15th year of the Republic of China. Later, he served as the Director of Education in Anhui, Hubei, and other provinces. At this time of national crisis, Ambassador Cheng has assisted the central government in its work to revitalize the nation, which is a great contribution. Now, Ambassador Cheng is about to go to Germany. This trip is not only to promote friendly relations between China and Germany, but also because Germany, after the European War, was a defeated country that was completely destroyed. In just a few years, it has risen again. Although its race is different from ours, its great national spirit and tenacious national character are of great value for our country to learn from. Therefore, I hope that Ambassador Cheng will take responsibility and introduce everything about that country to serve as a mirror for our national revival, and also hope that he will publicize the current situation of our country's efforts to govern and revitalize the country to friendly countries in Europe, and so on.

Ambassador's Reply: Ambassador Cheng replied, saying that he has served in education and party affairs in the past, and is now ordered to be the ambassador to Germany. Because of the lack of experience, he is very apprehensive. I hope that everyone present will give me advice from time to time. Regarding our country's diplomatic policy, President Jiang and Foreign Minister Zhang have repeatedly clarified it. I will do it according to this policy. I would like to offer some opinions as follows. In the past, some people advocated the diplomatic strategy of "using barbarians to control barbarians," but I secretly believe that our country's diplomacy for thousands of years has adhered to the principles of peace and friendship. During the Spring and Autumn and Warring States periods, academic thought flourished, and various schools of thought arose. The main schools of thought, such as Confucianism, Taoism, and Mohism, all opposed war, advocated peace, and sought to establish harmonious and friendly relations between countries. This kind of thought, even to this day, is still lurking in the national consciousness and has not changed slightly. Mozi advocated "universal love," which is the best policy for establishing international relations. It is certainly inappropriate to harm others to benefit oneself, and it is impossible in reality to harm oneself to benefit others. If both people and oneself can benefit, it is most appropriate. Therefore, in my opinion, if it can benefit both people and oneself and be applied to international relations, then international peace is promising. Germany's environment after the European War was worse than our country's current situation, but in just over ten years, its national strength has been steadily improving and has almost recovered to its pre-war strength. Its national spirit is great and outstanding, and its hard work and struggle are worthy of our imitation. This time I go, I will introduce the situation in that country in detail, and I will publicize the real situation of our country to friendly countries at any time. Since the German delegation came to China in the 19th year of the Republic of China, the relationship between China and Germany has become closer, and there has been more economic and cultural contact. In terms of economy, this year there is the organization of the Sino-German Trade Association. In terms of culture, Chinese classes have been added to German universities, and the Far East Association has been established. Our country also has the organization of the Sino-German Cultural Association, and many students go to Germany every year. The most fortunate thing is that several German universities will exchange students with Tsinghua University in our country. This is still an initiative, which shows that the relationship between China and Germany is becoming closer. Our country is rich in products and has a long history of culture, while Germany has a brilliant science and developed machinery. If these two countries and nations with their own advantages can work together, then the bright future will be boundless, and so on.

Wang Xiaolai's Speech: Wang Xiaolai said in his speech that the saying "a weak country has no diplomacy" is inappropriate. If a country considers itself weak, then there is no hope. Therefore, diplomats should uphold their indomitable spirit and negotiate diplomatically. Even if diplomacy fails, the individual diplomat will never fail. Weng Zhilong said in his speech that he hoped that Ambassador Cheng would introduce everything about Germany as much as possible and at the same time publicize everything about our country to foreign countries. The guests and hosts enjoyed themselves until 9 pm and then dispersed, it is said.

Ambassador to Germany Cheng Tianfang is about to leave the country to take office. Last night at 9 pm, Minister Kong specially sent Finance Decision Xu Kan as a representative to give him a farewell dinner at the International Hotel, and invited Zhong Wei Tan Zhen, Fu Rulin, Fu Bingchang, Lv Guang, Peng Xuepei, Tang Haian, and Chen Gongbo to accompany him. The host and guests dispersed at 11 pm.

Postal and Telegraph Agency Offices to Be Established at Major Stations on Both Railways; Ministry Order Approved, to Be Implemented on New Year's Day Next Year

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration previously received an order from the Ministry of Communications to set up postal and telegraph agency offices at stations. The draft outline of measures proposed by the Ministry has been consulted with the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau and the Shanghai Postal Bureau, and provisional measures for setting up postal and telegraph agency offices at stations on both railways have been formulated. After approval by the Ministry, it is scheduled to be implemented starting on New Year's Day next year. Details are recorded as follows:

Trial Implementation at Nine Stations

Location: To be attached to the appropriate locations within each railway station, temporarily to be piloted first at the five stations of Shanghai North, Shanghai South, Nanjing, Xiaguan, and Hangzhou City Station, Suzhou, Wuxi, Changzhou, Zhenjiang, Jiaxing and other five stations. The location of the agency office within each station will be designated by the Railway Bureau. To the extent possible, the agency office must have two doorways, one near the ticket office and one next to the platform, so that passengers in the waiting room and on the train can send and receive mail and telegrams at any time. Two wooden signboards will be specially installed at each office, one hanging in a prominent position on the platform and one hanging above the door of the agency office. The size and method of hanging the signs will be designated by the Railway Bureau. The color will be black with white letters. The cost of making and installing the signs will be borne by the Railway Bureau. The equipment costs required by the agency office will be borne separately by the two bureaus, and a mailbox or letterbox will be attached, the location of which will also be designated by the Railway Bureau.

Stipulated Duties

The office hours of the agency office are the same as the normal office hours of the station. However, in order to facilitate the sending and receiving of mail and telegrams from the outside, the agency office should make a sign showing the start and end times of receiving and sending various mail and telegrams and hang it at the door. The detailed times will be determined by the Railway Bureau. The duties of each agency office are to sell stamps, receive and send various ordinary registered express airmail items, and seal and dispatch parcels of mail to other places. The decision on the classes for sealing and dispatching parcels of mail at each agency office should be based on the trains with railway post office chiefs. The deadline for opening the mailbox and letterbox is fifteen minutes before the departure of the train. The deadline for sealing and dispatching is so that it can catch the train. When receiving and sending mail, in addition to ordinary mail, other registered express mail, etc., a receipt must be issued at the time of receipt and sent to the sender for safekeeping. There are three copies of the receipt in total: the first copy is given to the sender, the second copy is pasted on the back of the relevant mail item, and the third copy is kept as a stub. The first and third copies must be signed and sealed by the person handling the mail item and stamped with a date stamp.

Measures for the Two Railway Bureaus to Encourage Merchants to Ship Goods Directly

The Ministry of Railways previously believed that the method of giving rebates to forwarding agents by the railways was inconsistent with the original intention of responsible transportation of goods. The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus discussed and drafted provisional measures to encourage merchants to ship goods directly. The draft has been reviewed in detail by the Traffic Department of the Railway Bureaus and reviewed by the Accounting Department, and then submitted by the Railway Bureaus to the Ministry of Railways for approval under No. 1090, to be piloted for one year starting from January 1 next year. The measures are recorded below. Article 1: All merchants who ship goods directly to the Beijing-Shanghai Railway or the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway of this bureau and enjoy the stipulated benefits shall first register with the bureau separately in accordance with the regulations. Article 2: When applying for registration, the name, organization, location, capital manager, and destination should be filled in detail, and a deposit should be submitted separately, 500 yuan in national currency for each railway. Article 3: The registration deposit shall be deposited in the bank by the bureau, and one decision shall be issued annually according to the bank interest rate. When the registration is cancelled, it shall be returned according to the receipt. Article 4: The registration deposit receipt is not allowed to be transferred, rented, or mortgaged. Article 5: Registered merchants whose total freight paid to each railway each year reaches 5,000 yuan in silver shall be given a rebate of 2.5 per mille by the bureau. Article 6: For goods transported under special agreements, the bureau shall give special rebates at its discretion, but the benefits of ordinary rebates shall not be enjoyed. Article 7: If half-price return empty items, the full joint transportation fee transported from other railways, and the other railway part of the joint transportation fee transported from this railway, have already enjoyed the public transportation discount benefits, or if the goods are transported as packages, various miscellaneous fees that are not within the scope of transportation, etc., shall not be rebated. Article 8: The settlement of rebates shall be one year from July 1 to June 30 of the following year. If the start is midway, it shall be combined with the next year if the estimated annual average number reaches the number stipulated in Article 5 from the date of registration to the end of the year, even if it is less than one year, but those who have cancelled the registration without being enough for one year shall not be calculated. Article 9: If any of the following circumstances occur, in addition to handling according to regulations, the full or part of the rebate may be suspended, or the registration may be revoked and the deposit confiscated, depending on the severity of the circumstances: using a false name, falsely reporting the name or grade of goods or carrying prohibited items, using a forwarding agent, bribing the bureau's staff, or other acts that are harmful to the bureau's reputation or business. Article 10: If a registered merchant needs it for business purposes, the bureau shall give a free official passenger ticket at its discretion, but it must reach the amount of transportation in these provisional measures to enjoy it. Article 11: Registered merchants may also use the following measures: prepayment deduction or this railway transportation account settlement method, use of checks to pay freight, free mailing of freight receipts, and handling of pick-up and delivery matters. Article 12: In order to promote cooperation between the railway and merchants, all registered merchants may join the Railway-Merchant Liaison Association organized by the bureau as members, (a total of sixteen articles, omitted below)

Yu-Style Chinese Typewriter Offered as a Contribution to Flood Relief

The Yu-style Chinese typewriter was invented by Yu Binqi, a mechanical engineer who studied in Japan. It was granted Patent Certificate No. 18 by the Ministry of Industry and has been supported by dignitaries and business tycoons of the National Government. Not only are many domestic institutions, organizations, and firms using it, but also countries such as Britain, the United States, Germany, and Japan are buying it. In the last two years, more than 500 units have been sold. Mr. Yu believes that the floods in various provinces this year are serious, and that it is urgent to provide relief in this severe winter. He specially visited Mayor Wu and Section Chief Li of the Municipal Government yesterday, expressing his willingness to donate 15 yuan in national currency for the invention rights interest and 10 yuan in national currency for the business profit of each Yu-style Chinese typewriter that he personally invented. From today until the end of February next year, during these two months and more, a total of 25 yuan will be extracted from each unit to be used for flood relief in various provinces. The original price of the machine, 300 yuan in national currency, will be reduced to 255 yuan. He hopes that people from all walks of life will make resolute purchases during this period to do good deeds. It is said that the machine is guaranteed for ten years, and can be exchanged for one-third of the original price after the expiration, not for profit.

The Chinese and Foreign Relief Association Appeals for Winter Relief for Flood Victims

The Chinese and Foreign Relief Association on Renji Road has already been providing relief for floods. However, the area of ​​the Yellow River flood has expanded, funds are stretched, and time is long. Now that the weather is severe, the disaster is even more tragic. Therefore, winter relief is urgent. Yesterday, an appeal was made to all walks of life, issuing the following circular: "The drought was suffered in the spring, and the service has just ended. In the summer, before the crops were harvested, the floods came again. At first, the Yangtze River flooded, and then the Yellow River repeatedly reported breaches. As the Yangtze River subsided and the Yellow River rose, the disaster area increased and expanded day by day, and the number of starving people increased. The tragic scene occurred one after another, which is heartbreaking. During this time, the association has exhausted its funds due to the spring relief. Whenever it is difficult to advance or retreat, the directors have to take out their pockets to make up for the shortfall. Now that the disaster has been added to the disaster, how can we bear to see the death and not save it. Fortunately, we have received the enthusiasm of kind people at home and abroad, and have indeed received a lot of help, so we can gradually and reluctantly carry out relief matters. The outbreak started in Hubei, and the first shipment was medicine and cotton. Then, we worked with Jishenghui to provide relief in Tianmen, and then jointly with the Red Swastika Society to provide relief in the disaster area along the Yangtze River, so that we could go from Hubei to Hunan. We also gave priority to Hunan, and the association sent Director Lu Bohong to carry funds to choose Yun to investigate and release funds to supplement the insufficient funds. (Northern Jiangsu) Xu Province has always been poor. This time, the Yellow River disaster was repeated, and the tragic scene was repeated. The association sent President Rao Jiaju to personally inspect and observe. The drought relief office in Peixian had not been withdrawn, so we continued to release flood relief. Moreover, we considered that one relief office could not reach all areas, so we specially established a branch association in Yaowan to provide relief to Pizhou and Suqian. The Yellow River flood extended to the coastal area. On one side, we cooperated with Jishenghui to provide relief in Haizhou and Shuyang. (Shandong) The county established a branch association in Jining, and has provided relief to Juancheng, Yuncheng, Juye, Yutai, Heze, Jinxiang, Dongping, and Shouchang counties. (Anhui), Northern Anhui is suffering from a unique drought. Limited to the amount of cotton, it has been allocated to Huoqiu to choose Yun for relief. (Guangdong) Choose Yun for relief in Sihui, Guangning, and other areas. (Fujian) A Sino-Western committee has been established in Quanzhou to carry out relief work. In addition to the clothes and medicines transported by overseas Chinese and donated by all walks of life, they are all transferred to the disaster areas at any time. This year, we have allocated more than 300,000 yuan in relief funds, and 30,000 new cotton clothes have been sent to the disaster areas one after another. However, it is like a drop in the bucket. Agricultural products have long suffered from being out of season, and it is not known when they will be restored. When the water dries up and people return, they have no clothes, food, housing, or utensils. Moreover, the weather is cold again. If winter relief is not prepared quickly, the previous relief will be in vain. People are the foundation of the country, and food is the sky for the people. Planting seeds must be taken into account. Before the matter has been done halfway, those who are in charge have exhausted their strength and are in a dilemma. Therefore, we have no choice but to appeal to kind people, hoping that those who can give money will give money, and those who can do their best will do their best. Let us gather sand into a tower and gather fur into a robe, and jointly participate in the charity to save the countless starving victims. (If you want to ensure that your children and grandchildren will have a long and peaceful life, quickly give money and rice to relieve hunger and cold) Now is the time, and there is no need to beg,"

A Homicide Case Caused by Idle Talk Concluded; Li Zhou's Death Due to Beating

Zhou, the wife of Li Laosan, a Suzhou man who lived in Shantong Cemetery Pier and made a living by boating, was chatting with a neighboring boat woman, Lu, at 12 noon on November 2 this year. The conversation involved the affair between Shen Baogen's wife and the monk Ni San, which was overheard by Ni, who questioned them. There was a quarrel, and Ni, in a fit of anger, gathered Zhang Liu, Monk, Pan Amao, and others to brutally beat Li, injuring her abdomen. Since the woman was pregnant, she died on the evening of the 21st after being injured. Li Laosan reported the situation to the Procuratorate of the Local Court, which sent personnel to examine the coffin. The Public Security Bureau detained the three suspects, Monk Ni San, Monk Zhang Liu, and Pan Amao, and sent them to the Local Court for interrogation. A public prosecution was filed for the crime of Article 277, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law. Judge Lu Hongze was appointed to conduct a trial, which was not concluded. Details have been reported in previous reports. It is now known that this case was again tried by Judge Lu at 11 am yesterday morning. Plaintiff Li Laosan appeared in court to testify about the previous situation, requesting that the law be enforced, and pursuing a private prosecution of 500 yuan. The three suspects, Monk Ni San, Monk Zhang Liu, and Pan Amao, who were in custody, were questioned. The interrogating official obtained a confession and invited Prosecutor Lei Binzhang to court. After the prosecutor made his opinion, the interrogating official considered the case to be concluded and scheduled a sentencing date. The defendants were returned to custody.

Seized on the Songshan Steamer: Three Human Traffickers and Two Abducted Boys Discovered

Recently, there have been frequent reports of child abduction in Shanghai's Hunan, Zhabei, and other areas. As a result, investigators Chen Shaoting and Lin Yongfang from the Shanghai Relief Association for Women and Children are diligently inspecting outbound ships to prevent human traffickers from escaping. Yesterday at 11:00 AM, the investigators went to the Laobaidu Wharf in Pudong, as usual, and boarded the Songshan Steamer bound for Xiamen and Shantou. There, they discovered human trafficker Zhao Yunfu (48 years old, from Hunan), and female trafficker Sun Zhangshi (28 years old, from Huzhou), who had abducted a two-year-old boy and planned to sell him in Shantou. When questioned by the investigators, Zhao, knowing he could not hide the truth, admitted that there was also an elderly woman, Wang Zhao, who was also bringing a seven-year-old boy to Shantou for sale. However, Wang Zhao had not yet disembarked. The investigators then notified the water police station, which dispatched detectives Liang Shenqing, Yao Guofa, Shen Changshan, and Qu He Kui. They arrested the human traffickers Zhao Yunfu and Sun Zhangshi, along with the child, and took them to the police station. Investigator Chen waited at the wharf. Later, he saw an elderly woman wandering near the wharf and approached her, asking if she was looking for Zhao. The woman said yes. He then asked where the seven-year-old boy was, and she replied that he was in a snack shop. Knowing that the elderly woman was Wang Zhao (44 years old, from Huzhou), the investigator apprehended her, along with the seven-year-old boy, and took them to the police station. In the afternoon, they were transferred to the local court for interrogation and legal proceedings.

Rickshaw Replenishment Registration: Municipal Council Has Not Yet Approved; Yesterday, Rickshaws Were Inspected in the Hongkou Area; Those Without Armbands Were Detained and Fined

The Shanghai Special District Rickshaw Association previously stated that among the registered rickshaw pullers in the Special District, over 40,000 were missing more than 20,000, which meant that the rickshaw companies could not rent out all of their vehicles. Therefore, they negotiated with the Municipal Council to allow for replenishment registration. However, two months have passed, and the Municipal Council has not yet approved the replenishment registration. Yesterday, they began inspecting rickshaw pullers' armbands in the Hongkou area. Those without armbands were immediately detained, and registered rickshaw pullers were brought out, and each rickshaw was fined 50 cents. The association has decided to seriously negotiate with the Municipal Council regarding this matter.

A Cook's Friend Dies in Confusion

Mr. Mou, the cook employed by Chen Qingping of 37 Yinheli, Fangbanqiao, Min’guo Road, French Concession, had a friend named Liao, 54 years old, from Chaozhou. He was generally referred to as Old Liao. He was destitute and often sought help from Mr. Mou. Liao was quite honest, and considering he was nearing sixty, Chen Qingping, his employer, felt pity for him being old and without support and often allowed him to eat and stay at his home. Yesterday (the 21st) at 4:30 PM, Old Liao suddenly began rolling around on the cook’s bed, groaning incessantly. The servants suspected he was suffering from heatstroke and immediately gave him "Ten Drops Water" and other medications, but they had no effect. They then called the police station, and the Shan Fire Brigade sent an ambulance to rush Liao to Guangci Hospital. However, it was too late. He was already dead upon arrival at the hospital. The police suspected Liao's death was suspicious and had the body transported to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Hall on Ningbo Road, pending a report to the Second Special District Local Court for a coroner's examination.

Robbery Case on Xizang Road: Real and Fake Guns All Present; Zhang Jirong Alert but Suffers; Detectives Arrive Too Late

Chen Jirong, 21 years old, from Ningbo, resides at No. 73, Lane 246 (Yonghe Fang), North Xizang Road. Yesterday at approximately 6:00 PM, six men suddenly went to Zhang's residence and knocked on the door. When the servant opened the door and asked their purpose, they claimed to be public officials who had received a tip and were there to search for drugs. At the time, Zhang Jirong found the situation strange and, unwilling to be falsely accused, asked them to produce proof of authorization and argued with them. Unexpectedly, they were robbers who, realizing their plan was exposed, immediately pulled out three pistols, threatening Zhang. Instantly, they became menacing, placed the entire family under guard, and assigned an armed robber to oversee them. The remaining robbers swarmed upstairs, dividing into the various rooms and searching thoroughly, turning over boxes and cabinets without leaving anything untouched. After about an hour, they began to come downstairs one after another. Although Zhang Jirong was under guard, he paid close attention to the actions of each robber and discovered that the weapons used by the robbers assigned to guard Zhang and others were counterfeit. Therefore, Zhang Jirong grew bolder and, seeing that the robbers were about to leave, followed them, shouting "Catch the robbers!" Zhang's family also joined in the cries for help. The robbers, realizing the situation was dire, panicked and turned around, firing a shot and fleeing with all their might. Unfortunately, the bullet struck Zhang's left leg, causing him to collapse to the ground, bleeding profusely. The robbers took the opportunity to escape in different directions. By the time the precinct police received the news and arrived, it was already too late. They reported the situation to the police station, who dispatched detectives to investigate and transported Zhang Jirong to the hospital for treatment, while also searching for the robbers in all directions.

Zhong Baoxin Abduction Case: Trafficker Sentenced to Three Years; One Defendant Admits to Finding Customers; One Defendant Acknowledges Receiving Twenty Yuan

Five-year-old Baoxin, from No. 35, Lane 640, Huade Road, was playing in front of his door at the beginning of this month when he was abducted by a man from Haimen, who conspired with his friends Qiu Sanbao and Xu to sell Baoxin to someone as an adopted son. After Zhong lost his child, he asked people to search everywhere, but there was no news. He reported the incident to the Yangshupu Police Station. The next morning, detectives Liu Changgen and Su Yinggen apprehended Lu and the other three, and rescued the child Baoxin, bringing them all to the police station. The child was returned to his father, and the suspects were sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xie fen presided over a continued hearing in the Third Criminal Court. Mr. Zhang Shizhu, a lawyer for the Municipal Council, stated that there were no other cases pending and requested that the defendants be severely punished according to the law. When questioned, Qiu Sanbao claimed that Lu Yongchang brought Zhong's child, wanting to sell him, and he did not know that he had been abducted. The rest of his testimony was evasive. Xu Asan claimed that he only acted as an intermediary to find customers and did not go when the child was abducted, pleading for leniency. Lu Yongchang's testimony was cunning and deceptive. The court stated that he had already admitted to entrusting Qiu and Xu to sell Zhong's child, and if they succeeded, he would receive twenty yuan, abandoning the rest. He was ordered not to change his story. Lu Yongchang was sentenced to three years in prison, and Qiu Sanbao and Xu Asan were each sentenced to six months.

Dentist Situ Bo Found Not Guilty in Lawsuit: Deceased Suffered from Septicemia, Not Caused by Tooth Extraction

Dentist Situ Bo has a considerable history in the dental profession. Two years ago, he established a public dental clinic downstairs in his hospital to facilitate treatment for ordinary people with tooth ailments. He hired another doctor to handle the medical work at the clinic. In May of this year, Mr. Wu's son went to the clinic for dental treatment and was treated by the doctor there, but it was not very effective. He was referred to another hospital for treatment, but it was also ineffective, and he died. Later, Mr. Wu hired a lawyer and filed a criminal lawsuit against Situ Bo in court. The court has now found Situ Bo not guilty, with the following reasoning: The question of whether the defendant should be convicted of negligent homicide depends on whether the plaintiff's son died as a result of the tooth extraction and whether the defendant should be held criminally liable. According to the plaintiff Wu Juncai's statement, his son Lianfang, 11 years old, went to the defendant for treatment of a painful tooth on May 1st of this year. The defendant extracted a baby tooth. On the 7th, he extracted a decayed tooth, and his condition gradually worsened. On the 13th, the defendant referred him to Tongren Hospital for treatment. The hospital stated that he had septicemia. Disinfectant injections were ineffective, and he died on the morning of the 15th. He believed that this was caused by the defendant's negligent surgery. The defendant stated that the plaintiff's son was treated at the affiliated public dental clinic. After my examination, Dr. You Wenzong extracted a tooth. Dr. You was responsible for all subsequent treatments, and I did not see him. The referral to Tongren Hospital on the 13th was also not done by me. Furthermore, the plaintiff's son had a foul odor in his mouth when he first came for treatment and had a history of toothache and eczema, which could have caused septicemia, and the dentist should not be held responsible. According to You Wenzong's statement at the police station, the child was in great pain when he came to the clinic, and his tooth ailment had probably been going on for a long time. I told the child's family that there was a lot of pus inside a molar on the left side, and the child had a large sore. Surgery was very difficult. We extracted two teeth, a molar, and a baby tooth. At the eighth consultation, we extracted the blood tooth because the child was in great pain. I tried my best to treat the child (as seen in the police station's reply to the court). This proves that the plaintiff's son was treated by Dr. You Wenzong at the public clinic, which is consistent with the plaintiff's claim that the first consultation was personally examined by Dean Situ Bo of the defendant's affiliated public dental clinic. The fact that he changed to Tongren Hospital for treatment on May 13th was also on the instructions of You Wenzong, as stated by the plaintiff during the second court session (November 30th). The defendant did not perform the treatment, so there is no possibility of criminal negligence. Furthermore, according to the Tongren Hospital's diagnostic report, the deceased Pengfang had suffered from eczema and had had toothaches several times in the past two years. This corroborates the defendant's statement that he noticed a foul odor and pus in his mouth during the first examination, and You Wenzong's statement at the police station that there was a lot of pus inside the molar on the left side. This clearly shows that the plaintiff's son had a pre-existing dental ailment, and his condition was quite serious when he sought treatment, leaving no room for doubt. Regarding this point, the defense argued that anyone who has suffered from eczema and toothache may have a hematogenous infection that leads to septicemia and death, and submitted dental medical books written by Professor Fukushima of Tokyo Dental College and Director Kanamori of Tokyo Imperial University, as well as health monthly publications as evidence. After careful review, the evidence is admissible. The plaintiff's claim that his son had no pre-existing illness is clearly untrue. Therefore, judging from the illness, it is also sufficient to prove that the plaintiff's son did not die as a result of the tooth extraction, which is credible.

Based on the above conclusions, the prosecution cannot prove the defendant's guilt, so a verdict of not guilty should be pronounced. Therefore, in accordance with Article 293, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law, the judgment is pronounced as in the main text.

Brothers of the Fan Family Sue; Detectives Obstruct Freedom and Publicly Insult; Caused by Eviction of Tenants Suspected of Drug Trafficking; Result: Handcuffed and Sent to Police Station Halfway

Fan Tingzhang, 35 years old, from Zhenhai, Ningbo, the owner and manager of the Laosongmao South Goods Store at the intersection of Huade Road and Jingzhou Road in the Public Concession, and Fan Wenzhao, 36 years old, the owner and manager of the Dalai Ink Factory at No. 12 Chongrang Lane, Fuzhou Road, are cousins. Recently, they jointly retained lawyer Sun Zuji to file a complaint with the Criminal Division of the Second Special District Court, accusing Wang Donglin, a detective from the French Police Station, of illegally handcuffing and obstructing freedom and publicly insulting them on the 6th of this month, requesting investigation. According to the complaint, Zhang Fan, Fan Tingzhang's sister and Fan Wenzhao's cousin, lives at No. 8 Youde Lane, Malan Road. In March of this year, their tenant Yu Xisheng was suspected of drug trafficking. After the police station sent detectives to search, they came to search again on the 1st of this month, but no evidence was found. However, the Zhang Fan family was frightened. On the 6th of this month, they evicted Yu Xisheng. Yu refused and instead gathered his mother-in-law, brother-in-law, and Xiang Tianbao and others to make trouble and use force, resulting in the plaintiffs' niece being injured. The case was sent to the police station for a fine. The plaintiffs, out of affection for Zhang Fan as their sister, went to mediate. Yu Xisheng then gathered hooligans to provoke and quarrel with Zhang Fan. Fearing an incident, the plaintiffs reported to the police station. On the way, the defendant suddenly appeared, handcuffed the plaintiffs without explanation, and took them to the police station. After finding no connection, they were released. The defendant illegally obstructed people's freedom and publicly insulted them. According to the complaint, the court, led by Criminal Division Chief Wang Gangxu, issued summons to the plaintiff's side to appear in court yesterday to investigate the plaintiffs. Fan Tingzhang and his lawyer appeared in court. Fan Wenzhao was absent because of a trip to Hankou. Fan Tingzhang stated that my elder sister, Zhang Fan, and brother-in-law, Zhang Weifang, run the Jinfengtai incense and paper shop on Xujiahui Road and live at No. 8 Youde Lane, Malan Road. Because the tenant Yu Xisheng was selling red pills, my sister evicted Yu after the police station searched the premises. On the 6th of this month, my sister asked Yu's wife when they would move. She replied that if they wanted him to move, they would have to say something nice. Otherwise, he would not only not move but would also refuse to pay rent in the future, leading to a dispute. My niece was injured and later went to the police station, where both sides were fined 50 cents. Later, my sister called me, saying that Yu's side was still going to send people to beat me. I went to advise them that afternoon and then went with my cousin Wenzhao. When we arrived at Youde Lane, we saw Yu's mother-in-law and uncle Xiang Tianbao and others fighting again. Fearing a disaster, I ordered my clan member Fan Xingbiao to go outside and call the police. They were taken to the police station. Unexpectedly, as we approached the tiger stove in front of the intersection of Malan Road and Kangti Road, the defendant arrived with ten others in a rickshaw. When they saw me, they got out of the rickshaw and said I was a hooligan from Hongkou pretending to be a detective, and immediately handcuffed my brother and me. I repeatedly stated that I was a businessman and had not committed any crime and presented my business card for inspection. However, the defendant paid no attention and ultimately handcuffed us to the police station. After confirming that we were indeed legitimate businessmen, we were released. The defendant publicly insulted and obstructed our freedom, requesting an investigation. If there is any false accusation, I am willing to accept the punishment. After verifying the testimony, the court ordered that the hearing be rescheduled for 2:00 PM on the 28th of this month. It is noted that the plaintiffs, in addition to running their businesses, also serve as committee members in commercial organizations and are quite wealthy. They feel deeply humiliated by this unprecedented incident. In addition to filing a lawsuit according to law, they have also sent letters to the clan association and the Chinese Ratepayers' Association, requesting assistance in clearing their name.

British Company Public Buses on All Routes Will Increase Prices from New Year's Day

Due to the currency reform, the price of gasoline has soared, so the British China General Omnibus Company has decided that from January 1, 1936, the fares for all routes except Route 9 (because Route 9 has already increased prices twice), such as Routes 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, and 10, will be uniformly increased. One stop will be 10 cents, two stops will be 15 cents, three stops will be 18 cents, four stops will be 24 cents, and five stops will be 30 cents. Furthermore, for the double-decker buses that operate on Route 1, the fare for the upper deck, regardless of distance, will be 6 cents higher than the lower deck. From January 1, the fares for the upper and lower decks will be the same. It is also heard that after this fare increase, there will be no further price increases.

Wuzhou Gubeng Soap and Medicine Factory Carelessly Caught Fire Yesterday Morning; Fortunately, Only the Pharmaceutical Section and a Small Warehouse Were Burned; Pharmaceutical Production Has Been Temporarily Moved to the Second Factory to Continue Production as Usual

The pharmaceutical section of the Wuzhou Gubeng Soap and Medicine Factory in Xujiahui accidentally caught fire at about 1 a.m. yesterday. Various fire brigades gathered to put out the fire, which was completely extinguished. It was found that only the pharmaceutical section and the lower-level small warehouse were destroyed. The main soap manufacturing and other sections were not affected. It is reported that the factory has decided to temporarily move the pharmaceutical section to the second factory to continue production as usual.

The Lawsuit Against Zhang Ruizhen's Sister for Disputing the Will Has Been Decided

Ms. Zhang Ruizhen, a native of Minhou who served in the education sector, had considerable savings during her lifetime. In the summer of this year, she was hospitalized for treatment due to illness. Knowing that she would not recover, she invited her classmates to make a will, stipulating that if anything unexpected happened, all of her property would be inherited by her younger brother, Zhang Xifan. However, before ten days had passed, Ms. Zhang passed away, and Zhang Xifan filed a lawsuit in the local court to validate the will. However, Zhang's eldest sister, Zhang Meizhen, and others accused Xifan of forging the will and should lose the right of inheritance. The siblings sued each other, and Judge Pang Shurong repeatedly summoned witnesses and gathered information to reach a final conclusion. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. Now, it is known that Judge Pang has announced the judgment in this case: In the case of Zhang Xifan versus Zhang Meizhen and others regarding the validity of the will and the loss of inheritance, (Main Text) The oral will of the deceased Zhang Ruizhen is valid, except for the part concerning the loss of inheritance rights of the defendants Zhang Meizhen, Lin Zhang Shuzhen, and Li Zhang Wanzhen. The plaintiff's remaining claims and the defendants' counterclaims are dismissed. The plaintiff shall bear one-half of the litigation costs, and the remaining one-half and the counterclaim costs shall be borne equally by the defendants.

Chen Dimin's Family Has Many Problems; His Wives Have Filed for Separate Residence and Alimony One After Another; Wu Luo'e's More Than 5,000 Yuan Has Been Enforced; Tan Kunfan's Case for Separate Residence Has Been Approved for Postponement

Chen Dimin, a native of Anhui, who used to be a comprador for a foreign firm and owned real estate in Lafei New Village on Lafei Road, is 44 years old this year and currently lives with his father at 379 Baylor Road. He previously married Tan Kunfan (39 years old this year), a woman from Suzhou, and has been married for 20 years, with six children. They used to live together in their own house at No. 15 Lafei New Village. Later, Chen took a prostitute, Wu Luo'e, a woman from Suzhou and the younger sister of the former first Miss China, as a concubine and lived with her in Dazhong Lane on Tongfu Road. Not long after, Chen had another affair and abandoned Wu. Last winter, Wu first sued Chen for abandonment in the Second Special Court and filed a civil lawsuit for 16,800 yuan in alimony. As a result, the criminal lawsuit was dismissed as unfounded. She filed a separate civil lawsuit, and the first instance ruled that Chen should pay 4,000 yuan. Both parties were dissatisfied and appealed to the High Court. Chen lost the case. Finally, the appeal to the Supreme Court resulted in a final judgment that Chen should pay Wu Luo'e 5,500 yuan for living expenses. 4,200 yuan of Chen's property has already been seized for provisional execution. One wave had just subsided, and another rose again. On February 27 of this year, Chen and his wife had a quarrel and fought, injuring Tan's left eye. Because she could no longer bear to live with him, Tan took her six children and returned to her mother's house at No. 11 Dagu Road in Ningbo. She reported to the French police, filed a criminal public prosecution for injury in the Second Special Court, and also applied to the civil court for mediation for separate residence. Chen also requested mediation for cohabitation. As a result, the mediation on both sides failed. In the criminal case, Chen was fined 30 yuan and given a two-year suspended sentence, and he was ordered to compensate Tan 14 yuan for medical expenses. An appeal to the collegial panel was rejected and the original judgment was upheld. Now, Chen Tan Kunfan has returned to Ningbo with her children, and it has been ten months since her husband, Chen Dimin, has abandoned her and has not provided any support. Therefore, she has retained lawyers Jiang Yiping and Wu Baotai to file a lawsuit for separate residence against Chen Dimin in the civil court of the Second Special Court, requesting to recover the 700 yuan per month for living expenses from March 1 to November, a total of 6,300 yuan, and the 700 yuan per month for living expenses from December 1 onwards, as well as the return of the 3,000 taels borrowed for 20 years, totaling 4,195.8 yuan in foreign currency, and the overdue interest at a rate of 5% per annum. She requested that the defendant be ordered to pay all of the above and that provisional execution be granted. According to the complaint, the court summoned the parties to the Civil Court No. 7 at 3:30 p.m. the day before yesterday, with Judge Li Liang presiding. Both parties arrived with their agents, lawyers Wu Bintai and E Sen. First, the plaintiff Chen Tan Kunfan stated the subject matter of the lawsuit and the reasons for requesting a judgment, saying that her lawsuit was purely for the sake of her children. When questioned, the defendant Chen Dimin said that he was currently unemployed and that the property in Lafei New Village had been mortgaged to Hengye Company for 258,000 yuan, and he was really unable to pay the plaintiff's living expenses. He requested that the plaintiff's lawsuit be dismissed and that the plaintiff be ordered to take her children home to live with him. He had asked relatives and friends several times to persuade the plaintiff to return home, but she refused to return, and he had not abandoned her. The plaintiff said that he lied about not having money. He now has two cars and goes to dance halls every night. He also has a mistress and a small house outside. If he has no money, he can transfer half of the house and land to me. The land in Lafei New Village was originally jointly owned by me and him. Because he was doing mortgage, in order to save his face, I let him mortgage it. The defendant's mortgage will expire at the end of this month. If there is any surplus from the sale in the future, he is willing to give them half of it. If there is no surplus, there is no way. I only have one car, and the other is my father's. Although my father has some property, I cannot use it. Other than that, I have no shares. If any of my property is found, I can give it all to them. She is my wife, and I am very willing to reconcile and live together. The court verified the statements and urged the two parties to reconcile, but the plaintiff insisted on not agreeing, saying that if she lived with him again, he would hit her at any moment, and she was afraid that her life would be in danger. The court held that the plaintiff had not set a deadline for her future living expenses from December onwards, nor had she submitted an amount, and had not paid the litigation fees, so it could not rule on the basis of the above. It ordered the plaintiff to submit a deadline and amount and to pay the litigation fees. After thinking for a while, the plaintiff stated to the court that she would not request this part for the time being and asked for a judgment on the previous nine months and the loan. At this point, the two parties' lawyers stated that they, as agents, believed that the plaintiff and defendant had been married for many years and had many children, and they sincerely hoped that they would each make concessions and requested a reasonable period to conduct a reconciliation outside the court. The court approved the request and adjourned the hearing to January 10 for further questioning, and instructed both parties to conduct a reconciliation outside the court during the adjournment and adjourned the court.

The recent painting exhibition of the famous painter Wang Jiyuan opened yesterday at the Chinese Art Society at No. 45 Avenue Albert, French Concession. Minutes of the Accountants Association Meeting

The Shanghai Certified Public Accountants Association held its third board meeting yesterday at its clubhouse at No. 59 Hong Kong Road. The directors present were Wang Sifang, Xu Xu, Chen Riping, Wang Haifan, Qin Kai, Li Wenjie, Dong Chunbiao, Cai Yejang, Wan Ping, Bei Zu, Chen Xianmo, Xi Yushu, and Shen Xuejun. Jiang Wanping chaired the meeting, and the following cases were discussed: The Standing Committee of the Board proposed that any accountant who applies for membership must wait until they start their business, but the board meeting is only held once a month, and they cannot obtain membership immediately, which often causes counties to inquire and urge them, which seems inconvenient. It is proposed to consider a convenient method. It was decided to authorize the Standing Committee to conduct a preliminary review and verification and determine that they have obtained membership qualifications, and then submit it to the next board meeting for ratification. Committee Member Li Wenjie of the Preparatory Committee for the Construction of the Clubhouse reported that they had already purchased land in the New Urban Area in accordance with the resolution of the committee at Shanghai Bank and would sign the contract tomorrow. It was proposed to ask the board to nominate a representative of the association to sign the purchase contract. It was decided to appoint Director Wang Haifan to handle the matter together with the representatives of the Construction Committee of the Clubhouse. (Omitted). It was decided that the association should prepare various draft forms for members to apply for "registration" and "change of registration" and cancellation of "registration" so that members can request them at any time. It was decided to pass the resolution that the association's journal is usually published once every three months. Now, due to the slightly busy association affairs and more documents, in addition to publishing this issue in advance, the future publication will be irregular depending on the amount of information. It was decided to pass the resolution, but it should be published at least once every three months. Director Chen Riping proposed that the association should send new members various relevant accounting regulations and uniform styles, as well as laws and regulations concerning judicial treatment, and print them together so that they can follow them. It was also proposed to submit them to the National Association for deliberation and unified implementation. It was decided to pass the resolution and forward it to the association. Member Wu Ruisen inquired in a letter about holding the position of chief accountant of the public funds and public property management office in Changshu County, but it is an honorary appointment for local finance and is unpaid and does not seem to be on the list of civil servants. It was asked whether to apply for withdrawal from the association. It was decided to reply in a letter that since it is an honorary appointment and unpaid, it should not be subject to restrictions on concurrent positions. (Omitted). It was decided to approve the applications for withdrawal from the association by members Gao Zuying, Xu Chengzai, Hong Zhang, and Jiang Rutang. It was decided to approve the applications for membership by accountants Zhang Genglin and Deng Jiazhen.

Expansion of the Ophthalmology Department at Guangci Hospital

Since the completion of the new building of Guangci Hospital on Jin Shenfu Road, the original ophthalmology department has been greatly expanded. A special commissioner was sent to Europe to purchase the necessary equipment, and it is now reported that all of it has been installed. The hospital's consultation hours are all from 8 to 11 a.m. Recently, due to the overcrowding of patients and in response to the requests of middle and upper-class people, it has been specially stipulated that special consultation hours will be held every Monday, Wednesday, and Friday from 2 to 4 p.m. The consultation fee is uniformly 2 yuan, and the diagnosis and treatment will be personally performed by Dr. Lu Runzhi, the director of the ophthalmology department of the hospital. Dr. Lu graduated from the Medical School of Aurora University in this city. He served as a doctor at the ophthalmology hospital in Southern Vietnam and went to Europe for further study. He interned at various major hospitals in Beijing, Brussels, and Paris, France, and obtained many honorary certificates. Before returning to China, he visited ophthalmology departments in England, Germany, Austria, and the Czech Republic. He has extensive experience and exquisite surgery, coupled with the hospital's latest equipment, which is truly a gospel for patients.

The popular edition is priced at only 30 cents, and the special edition is priced at only 40 cents. Those who admire the writings of Changjing Hall should be among the first to read it.
