Shen Bao Local Supplement - Amateur Weekly

Amateur Anecdotes

The Future Trends of the Media

— Hualin

The brightness of society often relies first on the majority of upright and impartial media professionals to grind away at its "dark side," and then that so-called "brightness" will leak out a little news, until it reaches the realm of "light shining throughout the universe" and "radiance filling the sky." However, in these times when material desires are rampant throughout the world, most people can only think of benefiting themselves? If one can avoid harming others to benefit oneself, one can already be called a person of noble integrity in society, and few people ask about public welfare anymore. As a result, there is no right or wrong in the world, and black and white are often confused. Looking at today's political situation, economic conditions, and people's lives, the unhealthy aspects of the entire society's exterior and interior, and the dark forces that dominate it, are known to all knowledgeable people and can be spoken of by them. But who is responsible for breaking the "darkness" and pursuing "brightness"? I believe that at least the media should fulfill a part of the responsibility, especially in the current period when "freedom of speech" has been slightly "restored," its responsibility is even greater.

Everyone knows that journalists are uncrowned kings, the authority of public opinion, and their power is enough to deter the monsters in the dark corners. However, only those who can truly be "completely impartial and selfless," disregard "personal interests," and not fear "coercive sanctions" can then talk about the authority of public opinion, and only the doctor in Ibsen's famous work "An Enemy of the People" who is never subdued by power is the character we need in today's era of building public opinion. When those in power are obsessed with the moment, the result can harm the interests of the public, but if public opinion does not point out their misguided path, then the media's sin is actually even greater than that of those in power. For knowingly condoning them, personal dereliction of duty is a small matter, but the impact on society and the country is great.

In the end, public opinion must not only bear the responsibility of "destruction," but also bear the responsibility of "construction." If public opinion engages in "destruction" for the sake of "construction," then it is still worthy of being called "constructive public opinion." It is the duty of the media to add detailed criticism to events that have occurred or been discovered, explain their causes, study their history and environment, and deduce their results, but the main task of the media is to first use their true knowledge and insight to clearly recognize the right and wrong of events, or to use the power of public opinion to suppress them, so as to prevent them before they happen, or to use the power of public opinion to promote them, so that they can be realized. This kind of constructive advice is the highest goal of constructive public opinion.

Life

Students of Military Academies

— Gao Bang

More than a decade ago, wanting to wear a military uniform and a weapon belt, and strutting around as a military officer, I enrolled in a military academy.

"Camel Zhao" became our squad leader at that time. He wasn't particularly short, but he had a toad-like small belly sticking out, and his back arched upwards in the opposite direction. So, from behind, his head looked like it was embedded in his chest. This is how he earned the nickname "Camel Zhao."

"Camel's" face, it was said, used to be rosy and fair, quite handsome, but later he became ill due to being greedy with the food rations, so I thought his face looked as thin as a monkey's. His lips were barely enough to cover half of his teeth, and when he spoke, his lips and teeth came together, resembling a Buddha's hand. Therefore, whenever senior officers came to inspect, we couldn't help but laugh when we saw his Buddha's hand-like mouth.

"What are you laughing at? A soldier laughing? Only women and children laugh! Who's laughing again? I'll give them a beating with the board!" He would grumble at us like this when he saw us laughing, and actually using the board to beat us was a common occurrence.

His favorite thing to do was to give lectures, but we all got headaches as soon as we heard he was going to give one. When he lectured, he always repeated the same old lines. We only had to open the "Squad Leader's Lecture Summary" in the duty diary to see that what he said was just the same few points on it: one, absolute obedience; two, proper etiquette; three, neat housekeeping; four, endurance of hardship; five, physical training; six, ...

When we were doing field exercises and he saw onlookers nearby, he would have to give us the most severe lecture. He would become more and more energetic as he spoke, and if your posture was a bit relaxed, or if you weren't paying enough attention to his lecture, he would unceremoniously display his squad leader's authority in front of everyone, rushing over to you and hitting you a couple of times, or striking you on the back with his saber.

His temperament seemed to be naturally inclined to make things difficult for us. Every week, he held at least two rounds of cleanliness inspections and weapons inspections. He never gave people advance notice of when he would inspect, like a cat stalking a mouse, waiting for us to be having fun before suddenly barging in. He would be wearing a pair of white gloves, and as soon as he came in, he would feel the windowpane, squinting with his rat-like eyes. If there was a speck of dust on the white glove, then the student on duty in that room was in for some bad luck. He would either call you over, grab your ear and make you look, or rub the dusty glove on your face:

"Hey! Such clean glass? Good, confinement for a week!"

During weapons inspections, if he found a bit of oil in the barrel or that the cartridge hadn't been ejected, he would either beat you dozens of times with the board or make you kneel for hours.

I remember one week when only two students out of the several dozen in our squad weren't punished.

I lived in the military academy for over a year. Later, at the invitation of a friend, I took up the position of regimental commander in his unit. From that time on, I never heard any more news about Camel Zhao.

Social Science Lecture

How Relationships Between People Arise

— Qiu Sheng

When we talk about relationships between people, we easily think of terms like friends, relatives, spouses, siblings, etc., which indicate these relationships. If we ask how relationships like friends, relatives, and spouses arise, the usual answer is also very simple: for example, A and B become friends because they are neighbors or classmates or colleagues, or perhaps they become friends through a chance encounter. As for relationships like relatives and spouses, they naturally arise through marriage, or to put it more plainly, through sexual organs. However, relationships like friends, relatives, and spouses are only superficial relationships between people; and the above answers to these relationships are also very superficial. Everyone knows them, and we don't need to study them. We know that humans are social animals, living in society. The so-called relationships between people refer to social relationships between people; if there are no such social relationships between people, then society cannot be formed, and therefore humanity would not exist, and relationships like friends, spouses, and relatives would not arise. What we want to talk about here is the fundamental relationship between people, that is, how social relationships arise.

Bukharin said, "Society is organized by individuals, which is beyond doubt. Without individuals, there is no society – this is also very clear without detailed explanation. But it should be remembered that society is by no means a simple accumulation of many individuals. The total number of people, adding up Zhang San, Li Si, and many others, is not society. We already know that society is a real sum, a 'system'; we also know that in society, there exists a complex network of diverse interactions between many individuals. Why is this? This is because society is a whole, greater than the sum of its parts, that is, society is not the sum of its parts added together. Whether it is a biological organism or a mechanical object, all kinds of systems have interconnected actions between their internal molecules. For example, a certain machine or a simple watch, if we disassemble its various components one by one and then put those disassembled parts in a pile – that is their total number. But this is no longer a machine, no longer a watch. Why? Because there is no fixed connection here, that is, the various components that form this machine have lost a fixed interaction. How can these components become parts of a machine's whole? Because there is a certain configuration in common. The same is true in society. Society is organized by people. But if these people do not occupy a certain position in the labor process at a certain time, if there is no labor connection between these people in advance, then society cannot exist."

In this passage, it is shown that human beings form society through labor connections; that is to say, social relationships between people arise through labor; labor is the basic condition for social relationships between people to occur.

In fact, whether you like it or not, as long as you still live in society,

Page 20

, you cannot avoid having more or less contact with all the people in society. If you want to eat and wear clothes, you have to have contact with landlords, farmers, weavers, and owners of yarn and cloth factories, as well as merchants who transport and sell goods; if you want to live in a house, you have to have contact with architects, workers, and real estate companies, etc.; even if you need to use the toilet, you have to have contact with the people who empty the chamber pots (those with flush toilets have contact with other people). If all the people in Shanghai who empty the chamber pots stopped working, that is, if the people who empty the chamber pots suddenly stopped continuing their relationship with people who need chamber pots emptied, wouldn't that be a disaster? But so-called farming, working, doing business, and even emptying chamber pots are all labor. Therefore, the above-mentioned relationships are labor relationships, and they are also social relationships between people that arise from labor.

To be more specific, society has a strict division of labor, and all people in society must directly or indirectly participate in the social division of labor in order to survive, that is, all people necessarily live in this social relationship of division of labor and cooperation. Although farmers can farm and produce food such as rice and wheat, they must have workers make farm tools in order to work, they must have civil engineers and stone masons build houses in order to have a place to live, they must have weavers weave cloth in order to have clothes to wear, and they must have merchants transport and sell goods in order to obtain all the necessities of life; similarly, all other groups or individuals must have labor relations with other people in society in order to live. In "Mencius," there was once a Xu Xing who tilled his own land and ate, leading his disciples to Teng State, seemingly independent of human labor relations, practicing self-sufficiency. This seemed so "noble." But in reality, he was not living outside of the labor and cooperation relations of human society. Please see the following interesting dialogue between Mencius and a worshiper of Xu Xing:

"Mencius said: Does Master Xu necessarily plant grains before eating? He said, Yes; Does Master Xu necessarily weave cloth before wearing clothes? He said, No, Master Xu wears coarse clothing; Does Master Xu wear a hat? He said, He does; Who makes the hat? He said, It's made by potters; Does he make the pots and pans by himself? He said, No, he exchanges them for grain; Mencius said, Why doesn't Master Xu weave cloth himself? He said, It interferes with farming; Mencius said, Does Master Xu use pots and pans made by others, and cultivate with iron tools? He said, Yes; Does he make them himself? He said, No, he exchanges them for grain..."

From this, it can be seen that no matter how "noble" or "capable" a person is, they are necessarily living in social relationships between people; and what constitutes this relationship is the division of labor among human beings.

In our society, because of the advancement of labor technology, the greater civilization of society, etc., the social relationships between people are more complex and larger. But this also arises from the division of labor process of human beings. The emergence of trains, ships, airplanes, telegraphs, and wireless radios enables all countries on Earth to exchange goods and communicate news with each other, establishing close relationships among all people on Earth. However, trains, ships, etc., are products of human labor, and the transportation of goods by trains and ships and the transmission of opinions and news by wireless radios, etc., all rely on human labor. Therefore, the expansion of the scope of current world transportation and communication and human relationships relies on human labor. At the same time, due to the advancement of labor technology and the expansion of human relationships, not only can individuals not live independently outside of the labor relations of society, but even a country cannot exist independently outside of international relations. A very obvious fact, such as the League of Nations imposing an economic blockade on Italy, was enough to make Italy suffer. Recently, the U.S. is about to implement a blockade of oil and coal on Italy, which makes the Italian people even more frightened and angry; but this is not all, if all countries in the world sever all relations with Italy, then Italy would be in danger of not being able to sustain itself. What is the reason for this? The final answer is still because the advancement of dynamic technology and the development of industry have made the people of the world have close relations, and have turned the world into one piece, and no one, not even any country, can exist independently outside of this entire relationship.

Of course, we are not saying that apart from labor relations, all other relationships do not exist at all. In fact, relationships like those formed by humans due to similar thoughts and becoming like-minded, relationships formed by harmony of thoughts and temperament and becoming friends, etc., are all commonly seen by us. But we still want to firmly say that these relationships are all appendages of labor relations. First of all, the so-called similarity of thoughts and temperament is not innate, but a product of people's labor life. Only those whose labor life or living environment is similar can have similar thoughts and temperaments, and thus be able to form like-mindedness or friendship; otherwise, it will not be possible. The oil tycoon and the rickshaw puller have conflicting labor relations and different living environments, so they cannot have similar thoughts and temperaments, and therefore cannot be like-minded and friends. This is a fact that no one can deny. Furthermore, if humans do not labor and do not have labor relations, they cannot survive at all, and human society cannot exist at all. Therefore, the so-called like-minded relationship, friendship, and even marital relationship would not occur. Based on this reason, we still want to say that the relationship between people is ultimately caused by labor.

Because the relationship between people is generated by labor, and people cannot live independently outside of labor relations, all human phenomena have an inseparable relationship with us, and we should all strive to understand them. For example, the United States' purchase of silver and the war between Italy and Abyssinia have a great relationship with China's finance, industry, and commerce, as well as our lives, and we should all pay close attention to them. In addition, we should do the same for all other social phenomena, large and small.

Opinion

On "Freedom of Speech"

— Zhong Lu

In the Sixth Plenary Session of the Kuomintang and the Fifth National Congress, there was a resolution to "restore freedom of speech." Compared to the period before the "restoration," it is indeed better. However, we hope that the so-called "freedom of speech" is true "freedom of speech," and not "freedom of speech" under the hard to guess "according to law" and "proper"; at the same time, this true "freedom of speech" should also be realized immediately, because this is a problem that the people of China are urgently demanding a practical solution to, and it cannot be resolved by a resolution or a piece of official document.

Now, because the "national crisis" is becoming increasingly serious, there are calls for "sincere unity to jointly face the national crisis" from both the government and the people. The meaning of "sincere unity" here, needless to say, is the "sincere unity" of the people of the whole country from top to bottom or from bottom to top; because only when the people of the whole country are united with one heart can we resist a strong enemy and save ourselves from danger. However, to unite the people of the whole country to "jointly face the national crisis," at the very least, the general public should be allowed to freely express their opinions, they should be allowed to know the current situation at home and abroad, and they should be allowed to freely discuss ways to save themselves from danger. If one side is shouting "sincere unity" while the other side does not allow citizens with opinions to freely express them, and does not allow people who do not know the current situation at home and abroad to know these, then the so-called sincere unity will probably still be empty. Because we believe that at least during the current serious period of "national crisis," every citizen should be given more opportunities to understand their responsibilities, and they should be allowed to freely express their opinions and contribute their abilities in order to jointly save the country and themselves.

At the same time, the "restoration" of true "freedom of speech" can also strengthen our diplomatic power and increase the status of our nation in the international arena. Because if the people of our whole country can freely express their opinions, then it can show the high spirit of our people and the patriotism and self-love of the general public, making it impossible for traitors to forge public opinion to carry out rebellious activities, and making it impossible for aggressors to openly attack the people of our whole country.

Of course, the so-called "freedom of speech" should have considerable restrictions. But we believe that in the current situation, this restriction should be based on the interests of the nation and the general public. Specifically, the absurd remarks of Yin Ni and his colleagues and lackeys, and those remarks that please and flatter the enemy, should be absolutely restricted and absolutely prohibited; in addition, remarks that study all new and old academics, new and old thoughts, remarks that praise or criticize the reality of society, and remarks that express opinions on domestic and foreign affairs, etc., should be given absolute freedom, because only in this way can we show who is right and who is wrong among the various opinions of the people of the whole country, and can we promote the development of our country, nation, society, and culture. We believe that as long as someone does not think that their own thoughts are wrong, as long as someone does not think that their own thoughts must be despised by the people of the whole country, they will definitely not oppose this absolute freedom of speech, because the truth is not afraid of absolutely free discussion.

Recently, the National Government has issued an order to effectively protect public opinion. We hope that the true absolute freedom of speech as mentioned above can be realized immediately; in order to make this hope a reality, we also hope that all publishers, writers, editors of bookstores and newspapers and magazines, and the general public from both the government and the people, should pay special attention to this issue at present, and solve this issue with various effective methods.

Common Sense

The Role of Fire in Human History

— From Lu

Fire, this is one of the many great inventions that savage humans gradually completed from the experience of learning to use friction to generate heat. Chinese stories mention Suirenshi drilling wood to make fire, and all primitive savage peoples also knew how to use stone-on-stone methods to make fire. It can be seen that striking stones together to generate high heat for survival was a common knowledge of primitive humans. Of course, humans at that time were blindly using the physical laws of friction to generate heat for production. Therefore, they did not understand that this was a scientific principle, nor did they know that it was one of the scientific discoveries and scientific production activities. However, in any case, the discovery of fire objectively became a great step forward in the development of human physical science knowledge. Therefore, the discovery of fire must occupy a considerable position in the history of natural science because it shows that this physical law has been experienced by humans and that they have been able to utilize this law.

The invention of fire has extremely great significance for human evolution. This is a point that we want to particularly emphasize. First, we can see that the invention of fire has influenced the physical evolution of humans themselves. Before fire, humans' enjoyment of food was limited by the fact that many foods were difficult to split and chop, requiring sharp teeth to easily split and cut food in order to swallow it. This is just like carnivorous animals such as tigers, leopards, dogs, and cats, which must have sharp teeth for easy tearing of meat, while herbivorous animals such as horses, cattle, and sheep must have sharp teeth for easy cutting and chewing of plants. However, since the invention of fire, all foods that are difficult to split and chew can be cooked first to make them easier to swallow. Thus, the function of human teeth has been reduced. Therefore, humans do not need to have the sharp teeth of carnivorous animals to eat meat, nor do they need to have the strong grinding and chewing ability of herbivorous animals to eat plants. Although human teeth have degenerated and shortened as a result, they can eat more diverse foods due to the help of fire. On the other hand, before the invention of fire, humans had to have a very strong digestive ability to digest food, but since the invention of fire, food is pre-cooked with fire to make it a semi-digested product, which is easier to digest. Thus, human digestive organs have also reduced their function with the help of fire, resulting in considerable degeneration.

The invention of fire is also greatly related to the expansion of human food types, because without fire, teeth and digestive organs would have to adapt to certain foods and grow accordingly, which would limit their function. Certain teeth can only be suitable for eating certain foods, so the types of food are also limited. For example, carnivorous animals cannot eat plants and therefore cannot use plants as food, and herbivorous animals cannot eat meat and therefore do not use meat as food. These are very obvious examples. Only humans, with the help of fire, can eat all foods that can nourish them, so their food is particularly diverse and complex. As a result, they can obtain sufficient and numerous nutrients to nourish themselves, which enables humans to evolve and become intelligent and also allows them to have the possibility of fully propagating their species. This is because the quality of food is related to the progress of physical fitness and intelligence, while the breadth and quantity of food types can affect the convenience of the survival of the race, and thus also relate to the question of whether it can propagate.

The invention of fire was probably driven most importantly by the need for meat, but once fire was invented, it further promoted the development of meat-eating life. This development also promoted the expansion of fishing, hunting, and animal husbandry production methods. Therefore, Engels took the acquisition of a meat-eating life as a starting point, saying that it "produced two major results: one is the use of fire, and the other is the domestication of animals. With fire, the process of food digestion is reduced because food becomes a semi-digested substance after being processed by fire. With domesticated animals, there will be a constant source of food, and the milk of animals is no less nutritious than meat. From this point of view, fire and domesticated animals have opened up a path to liberation and progress for mankind."

While fire has very important significance for cooking, it is equally important for keeping warm. In snowy and icy conditions, especially in cold regions, it is difficult for people to survive without fire for warmth. Therefore, even though its role is not as generally effective in keeping warm as the invention of clothing, it is still an indispensable item for residents in cold regions for living at home and overnight. Without fire, humans would not easily survive and reproduce in cold regions. With fire, the area of human survival and residence can at least be partially expanded, and humans can thus have the freedom to migrate and live in extremely cold regions.

It is undeniable that the invention of fire has played the greatest role in the development of human production. This is because primitive humans initially used fire as an important tool for industrial production. Before the invention of metal utensils, the ability of stone tools to dig holes and cut objects was very limited, and felling large trees and building boats could not be done without fire. Savages burned down large trees with fire and also used fire to burn holes to make dugout canoes. Fire can be said to be the only powerful means of production for making primitive transportation tools. If we look at it from the perspective of the industrial development of manufacturing production tools, metal utensils and agricultural tools cannot be forged without fire. The development of finely fired pottery, used to hold water and grains, also cannot be fired without fire. Here, fire has become the driving force to advance humans from the Stone Age to the Metal Age, and the development of pottery also plays a great role.

Naturally, the transition from the Stone Age to the Bronze Age and even the Iron Age has also had an extremely great impact on the progress of agriculture, because the essence of agricultural tools can only be fully developed when they are manufactured with metal. Pottery plays a great role in storing seeds and grains. Therefore, the development of pottery also helps the development of agriculture. However, since the progress of metallurgy and pottery is related to the invention of fire, it is clear that fire also plays an extremely important role in the progress and development of agriculture.

Since the invention of fire required a very long and difficult experience, and its usefulness is so great, savages usually regard it as the most precious and sacred thing, and they strictly guard it and assign special persons to be responsible for its safekeeping. Therefore, this responsibility falls on women, becoming one of the original divisions of labor between men and women. Fire was very rare and difficult to obtain in primitive times, so primitive families gathered around a fire as a center, and the preservation of fire became the center of their gathering. The clan that lived together often regarded the rise and fall of the fire as its fate, so fire was regarded as a sacred object of worship, and the women who kept the fire were also imagined as goddesses in mythology. Hestia became the name of the goddess of fire in ancient times, and the fire in her temple was never extinguished. If the fire in other temples went out, they would go to her to get it. Stealing sacred fire was a sin and would be punished, and welcoming sacred fire also had certain religious ceremonies. The Roman sacred fire was preserved for thousands of years without being extinguished, and even virgins from noble families were chosen to protect the fire and never marry. "If the sacred fire is not extinguished, Rome will not perish" became their common belief at the time. This also proves how much the ancients valued and worshiped fire. Every Chinese family has a stove god, and temples also have so-called fire gods. These are all similar customs. The reason why fire is worshiped to this extent should be due to its great role in promoting human progress!

Book and Newspaper Reviews

Introduction to "World Military Affairs Illustrated"

— Dunru

——Published by Tuwen Publishing House, priced at three jiao per issue——

Because the world situation is increasingly tense, it seems that the smell of gunpowder and blood can be smelled everywhere in the world. Therefore, people living in the current world, as long as they are not muddleheaded "well-fed and doing nothing," are very concerned about current events under this tense situation. In this attention, they not only want to see written records about current events, but also want to see living photos of various figures in current events and concrete living situations of various current events. For example, when the Italian-Ethiopian war broke out, those who generally pay attention to current affairs naturally want to see all the written records of this event. But in addition to this, they also want to see the terrain of Ethiopia, the lineup of the Ethiopian army fighting for national independence, the true faces of Mussolini, Laval, Eden, and other figures, and the cruel situation of Italian planes bombing Ethiopia, etc. Therefore, recently, general political, economic, and cultural magazines and many daily newspapers, in addition to publishing articles explaining current events, have specially published some photos, maps, and cartoons about current events. Needless to say, this is of great help to general readers in understanding current events and recognizing the current tense world.

The recently published "World Military Affairs Illustrated" especially publishes current events, especially military photographs. We can see in it pictures that are sufficient to truly represent the important current events, so that we have a more profound impression and understanding of the current world changes. The publication has stated the reason for its publication in its inaugural speech:

"Countries are deliberately seeking progress in military equipment, and new weapons are invented every day. The mechanization of the army and the use of poison gas death rays will be powerful weapons in future wars. Countries are holding military exercises and air defense exercises, which are heard of every day. Taking lessons from others to seek progress, peeking at other countries' offensive methods, and devising self-defense strategies are something that soldiers should observe, study, and discuss, and the public should also prepare as common sense. Feeling that written records are not easy to popularize and create a deep impression, the World Military Affairs Illustrated is published."

Indeed, in a country like ours where everything is very backward, like our semi-colonial people, we should "take lessons from others" in all aspects to seek our own progress and ultimate way out. If "World Military Affairs Illustrated" really contributes some new scientific inventions, the real situation of the world powers preparing to kill, the terrain of important places in the competition between the powers, the photographs of the oppression of various small nations and their spirit of resistance, etc., according to its purpose, then it is bound to be loved and respected by general readers. It goes without saying.

The inaugural issue of this pictorial is a special issue on the Italian-Ethiopian War. In this issue, you can see various pictures showing the historical background of the Italian-Ethiopian dispute and the British-Italian conflict, Mussolini's ambition to expedition to East Africa, the relationship between the Italian army's actions and the Ethiopian climate, and you can also see the heroic spirit of the Ethiopian people resisting the enemy, a detailed map of Ethiopia, the importance of the Suez Canal, and the military confrontation between Britain and Italy in the Mediterranean. What I think is the most meaningful and difficult to see is several photographs of the Ethiopian people fighting the enemy with their entire families. Just from the facial expressions of these Ethiopians fighting the enemy with their entire families, we can already understand their inner feelings, how angry they are at the brutal aggressors, and how enthusiastic their burning emotions are for national independence. In addition, the explanations of the history, treaties, and current situation of the Suez Canal in words and pictures, the explanations of the geography, history, climate, products, and political economy of Ethiopia are of course necessary for Chinese readers who are not familiar with the situation in Africa.

Naturally, "World Military Affairs Illustrated," like other publications, also has shortcomings. Here we can mainly point out two points:

First, the attitude expressed by this pictorial is a bit unclear. It said in its inaugural speech: "The publication of this journal is in response to the needs of the times. What should be stated is that this newspaper is purely for introducing facts and does not participate in discussion; the materials are all based on sources, and the text is only for explanation. When things involve both parties, it is absolutely in a neutral position;..." In fact, there is no such thing as absolute neutrality in the world. The occurrence of all events in the world has its inevitable causes and possible results, and it has its realistic and great significance. As long as we want to talk about these events, we must have a certain position, otherwise we cannot talk about it; even the introduction of pure facts has a position, otherwise it cannot be introduced. For example, the introduction of the facts of the Italian-Ethiopian War is different from what Ethiopia introduces and what Italy introduces, and the introductions from Britain or France also have their own characteristics: why is this? Needless to say, it is because their respective positions are different. Therefore, we hope that "World Military Affairs Illustrated" will not imagine absolute neutrality, but will clearly stand on a just and upright position to introduce everything and criticize everything. Of course, this just and upright position should be a progressive position that sympathizes with the weak, because if "sympathizing with the violent oppressors, even the wise will become fools," because only by sympathizing with the weak can we gain the resonance of the majority and gain the majority of readers.

Second, because this pictorial imagines absolute neutrality, the text of the current affairs commentary is still too little. I think that although the pictorial should focus on pictures, it should also publish as much text as possible that is directly or indirectly related to the pictures; it is best to have half text and half pictures. Because pictures, especially those rigid photographs, can only give us an impression of the facts, while abstract text can fully express people's understanding of things and critical opinions, so that the general reader can have a clearer and deeper understanding of the facts. The effect of pictures is to give people a concrete and deep impression of the facts, while the function of text is to give people a critical understanding of things with abstract analysis. Pictures and text are both important to us. However, "World Military Affairs Illustrated" has very little text that criticizes and explains current events, and all that is available is short text that "only explains" the pictures: this cannot but be said to be a shortcoming produced by the pictorial being too pictorial.

However, in any case, "World Military Affairs Illustrated" is much better than those pictorials that specialize in talking about decorations to young mistresses and young ladies, than those pictorials that print semi-nude images of "standard beauties," and than those humorous and funny pictorials. Therefore, we still want to introduce to the general readers here: the publication of this pictorial under the current tense situation has its significance, and its content is certainly worth reading.

Scientific Talks

Soil-less Cultivation Method

— Shiyong

T. R. Malthus published the principle of population at the end of the 18th century, saying that "the rate of population increase follows a geometric ratio, while the increase in food follows an arithmetic ratio." His biggest argument is: "...Taking any number of humans in the world as a standard, such as 10 million as an example, after every 25 years, the number will double, such as the ratio of 1, 2, 4, 8, 16, 32, 64, 128, 256, 512, etc., while the proportion of food increase is 1, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10, etc. Therefore, after 225 years, the ratio of population to food is 512 to 10; after 300 years, the ratio of population to food is 4096 to 13; after 2000 years, although food will also increase greatly, the difference between it and the population is almost incalculable by numbers... Looking at it this way, we can see that the power of population increase exceeds the power of the earth to produce human living materials too much." Although the certainty of this theory has been severely criticized by many scholars, the trend of population increase is absolutely true. From Malthus's time to the present, only a hundred and several decades have passed, and this fact has gradually been proven by that principle, although not as serious as Malthus expected.

Since population increase is a fact, it has aroused the excuse of a group of militarists to encroach on other people's land and plunder other people's food, and they also have to say so skillfully: "Civilized people come to take care of the world."

In fact, is population surplus the only way out to take colonies and plunder food by force? No, no, definitely not! This is just a foolish act done by a part of mankind.

Since there is a fact of population increase rate in the world, humans should also think about how to increase food to adapt to the increase in population and to make full use of land.

Continued on page 5

Page 22

Page 23

Unfortunately, this task of scientists is by no means understood by a part of mankind. Recently, I received a letter from Tokyo from my friend Zhou Chengyuan, saying, "You can grow things without land." He said:

"The growth of plants only requires the following six conditions: water, air, temperature, nutrients, light, and the absence of growth-limiting substances. Therefore, even without soil, we only need to think of ways within the scope of these six conditions, and it is possible to grow things without land.

This issue has been studied a long time ago. About 236 years ago, the hydroponics method was invented. The so-called hydroponics method is to dissolve the nutrients needed by plants in water to form an artificial plant nutrient solution, and plant the plants in it to make them grow. However, because the initial experiments consumed a lot of money, time, and labor, it can only be regarded as an explanation of a theory.

Recently, Shinichiro Kasuga, an assistant professor at the University of Tokyo in Japan, has successfully tested this method.

Mr. Kasuga began to conduct research in 1929. He first experimented with rice, and the results were almost the same as those grown in ordinary soil. Later, he also cultivated wheat, cucumbers, eggplants, tobacco, peas, broad beans, sugarcane, tomatoes, morning glories, chrysanthemums, cucumbers, watermelons, lychees, soybeans, dahlias, passion fruit, impatiens, pumpkins, peanuts, taro, etc. using hydroponics, and the results were very good, even better than soil cultivation. Even the most difficult radish has been successfully tested. The problem now is how to apply it.

As for the implementation method of hydroponics, it is also very simple. Take a pot, put gravel in it, place the young plants you want to plant in it, and inject artificial nutrient solution. This nutrient solution is changed about every three to seven days. After about fifteen times, it can bear fruit and mature. However, because the plants planted are different, the nutrient solution used is also different. Now I will give an example of one of the nutrient solutions used by Mr. Kasuga's experiments:

Artificial nutrient solution for vegetable cultivation (the amount contained in one liter of well water, tap water, or distilled water)

Raw material medicine Nutritional content Amount

Ammonium nitrate Nitrogen 0.0575

Potassium phosphate Phosphorus potassium 0.0383

Potassium chloride Chlorine potassium 0.0430

Magnesium sulfate Sulfur magnesium 0.01450

Calcium nitrate Nitrogen calcium 0.01170

Ferric nitride Iron 0.01-0.04

A little dilute hydrochloric acid until the PH of the liquid becomes five, five to seven.

According to Mr. Kasuga's calculations, the cost of each pot of this hydroponics method is as follows:

Plant Medicine price Total daily Ordinary fertilizer

Vegetables 0.038 0.010 0.022

Rice 0.010 0.003 0.006

From the above table, it is very cheap economically...."

We hope that Mr. Kasuga's experiments can expand its effectiveness, calm down a few of the cruel hearts that are jumping violently in the world, and reduce a little pain for mankind. This is the only responsibility of scientists to save all living beings.

Literary Works

Raising the Account Book (8)

— Puyu

"Hey! Don't pretend to be dead, what are you going to do?"

The old man hesitated for a few minutes before bending his back and approaching me, choking and saying:

"Director Liu, you are still young, please do something good, - understand that I have made no mistakes," he said, arching his hands, "The number you said will really force me to death! Look at this..." He just handed over the account book, then opened the money box, "Look: - if you find 20 yuan, I am willing to be fined a hundred times, a thousand times! The 400 yuan the other day is still paying interest, - 5% interest! Well, well..."

This guy really knows how to pretend to be dead, and even shed tears. But what is the use? I have seen this situation too many times. To be honest, my temperament is a bit strange: the more others say they are poor, the more I always feel they have money. For example, the old man's account book does not have many incoming payments, and there is only a pile of copper coins in the money box, but I suspect that the account book is fake and the money is hidden in the cellar. Really, this is very possible, don't be fooled! Whoever has their throat strangled by me should not even think of taking a breath! (To be continued)

Quick Sketches of Characters in "Spring Flower"

Gao Zhanfei - A young military officer from a blacksmith's background, with a forthright personality, very fitting to Lao Gao's character. He married Yan Yuexian, a famous courtesan, and they have a daughter. After retiring from the military, he lived in poverty. Yan Yuexian, unable to bear this life of poverty, ran away. Then he lived with Huang Naishuang, worked hard and became rich. He was suspected of murder, fled to another place, and his whereabouts are unknown.

Huang Naishuang - Gentle, shrewd, and capable, she deeply sympathizes with the unsuccessful Gao Zhanfei, even sacrificing her fatherly love to marry Gao.

Yan Yuexian - A flirtatious and lascivious singer, good at dressing up. She first met Sun Min, then married Gao Zhanfei. Because Gao was poor, she eloped with Sun Min. Eventually, she ended up as a street prostitute. When she met Gao Zhanfei again, she was ashamed and committed suicide.

Sun Min - Originally a soldier with Gao Zhanfei, he was good at squandering money, quite like a young master with a fortune. He made a fortune by selling smuggled goods, so he retired from the military and became a gentleman living at sea. He lured Yan Yuexian to elope, but Gao Zhanfei discovered it, and they fought. He accidentally fell to his death.

Wang Xianqi - A ruthless merchant who does all kinds of evil, what Shanghainese call a "loafer." He loves to gamble and is a close friend of Sun Min. After Sun's death, he cohabits with Yan Yuexian. The wealth Yan brought with her was completely squandered, but his greed for money did not die. Later, he and his accomplices went to snatch Yan's young daughter, and was imprisoned for it.

Zhu Qiuhen - A movie star who is good at making trouble. Seeing her gives people a headache. She is the protagonist of the "Love Song Not Intended" in the play-within-a-play in "Spring Flower." When Gao Zhanfei fell into acting as an extra, he was mistaken for the male star she loved, causing many jokes.

Xie Yunqing - Huang Naishuang's father, who is blind. He is kind, but ultimately dies a tragic death.

Prelude to "Triumphant Song"

Following "Heroes of the Times", the honorable contribution of Yihua Film Company, the full-dialogue sound film "Triumphant Song", will meet you in major theaters both in and out of the city. Here, we sincerely recommend it to you.

"Triumphant Song" is a passionate poem, a tragic lyrical painting, an exciting bugle call, a movie with a soul and backbone, and also the crystallization of Bu Wancang's year of hard work.

The consciousness of "Triumphant Song" is correct. It grasps the reality, clearly showing a correct path to the drought-stricken countryside, exposing the darkness of feudal forces, dissecting the reasons why local tyrants and evil gentry manipulate the countryside to the point of being terminally ill. The director uses sharp techniques and tense moods to stimulate the audience, emphasizing the inviolable power of ten thousand streams converging to form a great tide. Therefore, "Triumphant Song" not only clearly shows that relief from disaster cannot rely on heaven or gods, but only on ourselves, but also implies that at this critical moment of survival, only the unity of the entire nation can save us!

The script itself has serious significance, plus the technical aspects—such as the arrangement of shots, the magnificence of the pictures, the application of techniques, the expressions of the actors, and the sets and sounds—have unexpected and pleasing results, naturally making "Triumphant Song" perfect.

We are confident that this "Triumphant Song" will not only surprise and amaze you after watching it, but especially will stir up a huge wave in this stagnant film industry—and even in this stagnant China.
